  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13815796882412594251">Spagna, Costa Blanca. il sole è ancora molto caldo nonostante sia già settembre inoltrato. Per le strade non c'è nessuno, e l'aria è pervasa da un intenso profumo di limoni che arriva fino al mare. È qui che Sandra, trentenne in crisi, ha cercato rifugio: non ha un lavoro, è in rotta con i genitori, è incinta di un uomo che non è sicura di amare. È confusa e si sente sola,</span>
  <span id="freeText13815796882412594251" style="display:none">Spagna, Costa Blanca. il sole è ancora molto caldo nonostante sia già settembre inoltrato. Per le strade non c'è nessuno, e l'aria è pervasa da un intenso profumo di limoni che arriva fino al mare. È qui che Sandra, trentenne in crisi, ha cercato rifugio: non ha un lavoro, è in rotta con i genitori, è incinta di un uomo che non è sicura di amare. È confusa e si sente sola, ed è alla disperata ricerca di una bussola per la sua vita. Fino al giorno in cui non incontra occhi comprensivi e gentili: si tratta di Fredrik e Karin Christensen, una coppia di amabili vecchietti. Sono come i nonni che non ha mai avuto. Momento dopo momento, le regalano una tenera amicizia, le presentano persone affascinanti, come Alberto, e la accolgo nella grande villa circondata da splendidi fiori. Un paradiso. Ma in realtà si tratta dell'inferno. Perché Fredrik e Karin sono criminali nazisti. Si sono distinti per la loro ferocia e ora, dietro il loro sguardo pacifico, covano il sogno di ricominciare. Lo sa bene Julian, scampato al campo di concentramento di Mauthausen, che da giorni segue i loro movimenti passo dopo passo. Sa bene che le loro mani sottili e rugose si sono macchiate del sangue degli innocenti. Ma ora, forse, può smascherarli e Sandra è l'unica in grado di aiutarlo. Non è facile convincerla della verità. Eppure, dopo un primo momento di incredulità, la donna comincia a guardarli con occhi diversi. A leggere dietro i loro silenzi, i sorrisi, le parole dette non dette, i regali. Adesso Sandra l'ha capito: lei e il suo piccolo rischiano molto. Ma non importa. Perché tutti devono sapere. Perché è impossibile restituire la vita alle vittime. Ma almeno fare in modo che tutto ciò che è successo non cada nell'oblio. E che il male non rimanga impunito.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13815796882412594251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_855853655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855853655" />
    <a title="Zoeytron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12656534-zoeytron"><img alt="Zoeytron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542977636p2/12656534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855853655?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoeytron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoeytron" href="/user/show/12656534-zoeytron">Zoeytron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846882432" href="/book/show/17399338-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12656534-zoeytron?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855853655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11504804437354551297">As a secret community of very elderly Nazis enjoy the good life in the Spanish coastal town of Costa Brava, an aging and ailing Nazi hunter is on their trail, gathering information to confirm their identities. His name is Julien and he knows that people don't really change for the better, they just get old. In this case, old age merely hides their evil. Julien is well aware that time is running out for justice to be served, but he simply cannot help himself from continuing to pursue it.<br/><br/>Sandra is</span>
  <span id="freeText11504804437354551297" style="display:none">As a secret community of very elderly Nazis enjoy the good life in the Spanish coastal town of Costa Brava, an aging and ailing Nazi hunter is on their trail, gathering information to confirm their identities. His name is Julien and he knows that people don't really change for the better, they just get old. In this case, old age merely hides their evil. Julien is well aware that time is running out for justice to be served, but he simply cannot help himself from continuing to pursue it.<br /><br />Sandra is also visiting Costa Brava. Although 30 years of age, she is fairly immature, pregnant, and wants to spend a few months by herself so she can figure out what to do with her life. Still not sure she should even have a baby, and not wanting to settle for the man who fathered her unborn child, she flounders. Befriended by the senescent Fredrik and Karin, Sandra is starting to think of them as adoptive grandparents when Julien makes himself and his theories known to her. He wants to enlist her help due to her proximity to Fredrik and Karin. It may very well be a game changer.<br /><br />For me, this was a slow read and uneven in the telling. The love story seems gratuitous and strains credibility. No idea on this earth from whence the title would have come; if there was even a thread of a tie-in, I missed it. On the upside, the characterizations were good, and I quite liked the ending. <br /><br />This was a First-reads giveaway, thank you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11504804437354551297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1365715500427148960">Firstly, I don't think the word "lemon" is mentioned in this book so I don't get the title. Until halfway through I was going to give it 2 stars because it is a good storyline that would make an interesting film. However, the writing is poor and it felt as though the author got bored towards the end of the book and just gave up so I took one star off. I didn't like the female lead character and I just found the whole series of events a bit daft.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_392666855" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392666855" />
    <a title="Beverley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8727567-beverley"><img alt="Beverley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334186783p2/8727567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392666855?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverley" href="/user/show/8727567-beverley">Beverley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846881855" href="/book/show/13512198-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8727567-beverley?shelf=disapointing">disapointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8727567-beverley?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8727567-beverley?shelf=nazi-themes">nazi-themes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8727567-beverley?shelf=haunting">haunting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8727567-beverley?shelf=prizewinners-and-nominees">prizewinners-and-nominees</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8727567-beverley?shelf=set-in-spain">set-in-spain</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392666855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer248935385371635874">2.5 stars<br/><br/>Reading this book is like going on a long journey where you're not sure if you'll reach the end, or if you want to. I went from loving this book, to being bored of it, putting it down, forcing myself to read the last 100 pages and being disappointed by the ending.<br/><br/>Lemon Leaves follows Julian, an 80 year old former Nazi war prisoner who receives a letter from his friend Salvo asking him to visit, as he believes he has discovered the whereabouts of a group of ageing Nazi war criminals. Upo</span>
  <span id="freeText248935385371635874" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />Reading this book is like going on a long journey where you're not sure if you'll reach the end, or if you want to. I went from loving this book, to being bored of it, putting it down, forcing myself to read the last 100 pages and being disappointed by the ending.<br /><br />Lemon Leaves follows Julian, an 80 year old former Nazi war prisoner who receives a letter from his friend Salvo asking him to visit, as he believes he has discovered the whereabouts of a group of ageing Nazi war criminals. Upon arriving at the care home in Spain where Salvo lives, he is informed of the sad news of his death. Determined not to give up and return home he attempts to find the Nazi's himself. He meets a surprising ally in Sandra, a young pregnant woman who is unknowingly befriended by the Nazi circle, she helps discover the secrets of the "brotherhood" by infiltrating them and living with 2 of the leading Nazi's. <br /><br />I was really struck how sinister the early part of this book was. The way the tension builds up is subtle yet quite unnerving in places. Despite this as I read on I became more and more frustrated. Once you've got over how horrible it is that these scum bags are living relatively normal, happy lives it doesn't seem to develop much further. I'm all for karma and these people getting what they deserve, even at this late stage of their lives, but that didn't happen. I know life isn't like a fairy story but Julian had enough evidence to send them all away to prison for the rest of their lives, but instead he leaves them to die of old age. It just didn't seem like justice. <br /><br />Throw into the mix one of the most poorly developed "love" stories I ever read and it's pretty hard going in places. <br /><br />The relationship between Julian and Sandra was well developed, but I disliked the way that the author replayed the same scene from both perspectives. It was dull to read and didn't seem to add a great deal to the story.<br /><br />Maybe i've been a bit too negative here. I love the originality of the idea, the creepy sense of foreboding and the development of the relationship between the 2 characters but it's just not enough. Something is missing here. I'm not sure what exactly, that spark that makes you want to turn the pages. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="248935385371635874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13774815107413448910">I really had to force myself to finish this book which, I have to confess, I only did so that I could tick it off my “books I’ve read” total for the year. Unfortunately it’s so far settled into my “worst book of the year spot”, from which I don’t imagine it will be shifting any time soon.<br/><br/>I was drawn to this book by the description – an aged Nazi hunter travels to Spain from South America after having been left some clues by a dead friend, whilst an unsuspecting young local woman is drawn into an</span>
  <span id="freeText13774815107413448910" style="display:none">I really had to force myself to finish this book which, I have to confess, I only did so that I could tick it off my “books I’ve read” total for the year. Unfortunately it’s so far settled into my “worst book of the year spot”, from which I don’t imagine it will be shifting any time soon.<br /><br />I was drawn to this book by the description – an aged Nazi hunter travels to Spain from South America after having been left some clues by a dead friend, whilst an unsuspecting young local woman is drawn into an unexpected new social circle… It’s an achievement, in fact, that with such fascinating subject matter the author managed to contrive such a ridiculous and one dimensional plot and characters. There’s no intrigue as the book is simply totally unbelievable. Both the “love story” and unmasking of the Nazis strands of the plot are risable.<br /><br />The English version of this book is a translation from the original Spanish which may be a contributing factor for the dull prose, which just hammered its way through the plot no more elaborately than if it were a shopping list or instruction manual for an electronic device. <br /><br />Overall, a very disappointing and frustrating read.</span>

<div id="review_384284489" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384284489" />
    <a title="Sam Still Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162915-sam-still-reading"><img alt="Sam Still Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232938717p2/162915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384284489?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Still Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Still Reading" href="/user/show/162915-sam-still-reading">Sam Still Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846881855" href="/book/show/13512198-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those looking for something different</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sam Still Reading by: </span>
      sent to me by publisher - thank you
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384284489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4261527372640190263">The Scent of Lemon Leaves is translated from the Spanish and I’m so glad it was (as I’m sure my Spanish friend wouldn’t translate for me and my Spanish is limited to ‘hola’). It’s a beautiful book that transcends genres – it starts as a hunt for Nazis, grows into a friendship between two unlikely people, containing thrilling suspense and a look at relationships.<br/><br/>The book is told in alternate first person – starting with Julian. Julian is a former inmate of the Nazi concentration camps and he and </span>
  <span id="freeText4261527372640190263" style="display:none">The Scent of Lemon Leaves is translated from the Spanish and I’m so glad it was (as I’m sure my Spanish friend wouldn’t translate for me and my Spanish is limited to ‘hola’). It’s a beautiful book that transcends genres – it starts as a hunt for Nazis, grows into a friendship between two unlikely people, containing thrilling suspense and a look at relationships.<br /><br />The book is told in alternate first person – starting with Julian. Julian is a former inmate of the Nazi concentration camps and he and his friend, have been trying to hunt the officers down over the years. Julian returns to Spain from Buenos Aires after a letter from his friend Salva about an infamous Norwegian Nazi couple living there. On arrival, Julian finds Salva is dead. If he wants these people to come to justice, it’s up to him. Enter Sandra. Sandra has fled her partner after finding she is pregnant – she’s not sure what she wants. Coming over ill on the beach one day, she is rescued by Fred and Karin, who happen to be the people Julian is hunting. As Sandra is brought deeper and deeper into the Brotherhood, she and Julian become friends to try and discover what is going on. Although these people may be elderly, they certainly have the power to try and dissuade Julian and Sandra by fear.<br /><br />Although the cover may not look like it, this book is quite a thriller, especially once Sandra realises her wannabe grandparents are high ranking Nazis. There were times that I just couldn’t stop reading, wanting to know what happened next. At other times, this book moves more slowly, exploring the friendship between Julian and Sandra and how they can help each other. The book also looks at other relationships too – such as Julian and his daughter, Sandra and her unborn son and the power play between those in the Brotherhood. It’s also an interesting relationship between the past and the present. The past hangs heavily on the characters’ minds – for Julian, it’s bringing the Nazi officers to justice on behalf of those who didn’t make it to old age and for the Brotherhood, it’s trying to regain lost glories and stop the ageing process.<br /><br />There’s a lot of talk about age and its effects on the body. We know repeatedly that Julian needs to take a lot of medication to keep functioning and Sandra is horrified at how skinny he is. Alice, one of the Brotherhood, looks oddly young for her age and Karin is riddled with arthritis. It’s interesting that some of the main power plays and arguments between the Brotherhood take place over medication. The reader is asked to judge if given that these people who committed crimes are now old and falling apart, should they be brought to justice? What should be the outcome for them? Julian’s ultimate decision I found both acceptable in ways and unacceptable in others.<br /><br />I enjoyed how the novel ended. It wasn’t as I’d predicted and the winding down was symbolic of the ageing process. Definitely an enjoyable read with some unexpected twists.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://samstillreading.wordpress.com">http://samstillreading.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4261527372640190263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer561884805" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13333638854635437995">Maybe the stupidest book I've ever read. The author takes you on a 400 page trek and it amounts to nothing. It was like doing the big shop before Christmas, spending two hours in the supermarket and then it turns out you've forgotten your wallet - it was all for nothing! <br/><br/>I feel like the author wanted to write about the horror of the Nazis and how there are still people who follow their ideology etc, but it just felt undernourished - like she picked a subject and didn't spend a tremendous amount </span>
  <span id="freeText13333638854635437995" style="display:none">Maybe the stupidest book I've ever read. The author takes you on a 400 page trek and it amounts to nothing. It was like doing the big shop before Christmas, spending two hours in the supermarket and then it turns out you've forgotten your wallet - it was all for nothing! <br /><br />I feel like the author wanted to write about the horror of the Nazis and how there are still people who follow their ideology etc, but it just felt undernourished - like she picked a subject and didn't spend a tremendous amount of time researching it, I felt at times the author knew as little as Sandra herself knew.<br /><br />Sandra. Ah, Sandra. The stupidest character I've ever come across in all my years of reading. She didn't know if she was coming or going. She behaved like a fool. Don't even get me started on the ridiculousness of the 'love' story between her and Alberto. Mind numbingly boring and positively ridiculous. <br /><br />The ending was a joke. The pages were filled with repeat lines about what Julían or Sandra had eaten, medication and ails of the elderly and pregnant. The idea itself had plenty of potential but sorry to say that the author was unable to execute it with an effect. Maybe the translation from Spanish to English was poor but given the amount of one and two star ratings in Spanish, I doubt it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13333638854635437995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9859667247024866064">I received this book through Goodreads- first Reads. I am very glad I did not pay money for this book. It was a huge disappointment. I was expecting drama and intrigue, instead what I got was a play by play report on what an eighty-something year old man had to eat. The other narrator of the story, Sandra, was pretty much useless. The only interesting thing she did was steal the ampoules so that Juliann could have the contents analyzed. After meeting Alberto, aka The Eel, Sandra takes an immedia</span>
  <span id="freeText9859667247024866064" style="display:none">I received this book through Goodreads- first Reads. I am very glad I did not pay money for this book. It was a huge disappointment. I was expecting drama and intrigue, instead what I got was a play by play report on what an eighty-something year old man had to eat. The other narrator of the story, Sandra, was pretty much useless. The only interesting thing she did was steal the ampoules so that Juliann could have the contents analyzed. After meeting Alberto, aka The Eel, Sandra takes an immediate dislike to him. Then he manipulates a date out of her, kisses her, and then *Bam* she's in love with him?! I don't even think you can blame the pregnancy hormones on that. I found this character to be very selfish and just plain stupid.<br /><br />The entire story was very slow. It dragged on with unnecessary narrative. Also a lot of it was repeated over and over. I think you could gather all the elderly characters in the story and make them do a three legged race and it would be faster moving the story itself. Certainly, it would be whole lot more entertaining.<br /><br />Then after slogging through it, I find out it was all for nothing! There is no resolution to story. In fact, there doesn't even seem to be a point to it. Needless to say, I was relieved to have it over and done with. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9859667247024866064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_562654018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846882432" href="/book/show/17399338-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562654018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1084364798770404660">Can't believe how many 5 star reviews this book has. Some reviewers described nail-biting suspense and I wondered why? For me the story was totally implausible and incredibly boring and I couldn't get round to finishing the book as I found I couldn't care less what happened at the end. Sorry Clara, not my cup of tea. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1581504214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1581504214" />
    <a title="Val Robson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46500234-val-robson"><img alt="Val Robson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475704110p2/46500234.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1581504214?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val Robson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val Robson" href="/user/show/46500234-val-robson">Val Robson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846882432" href="/book/show/17399338-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46500234-val-robson?shelf=owned-given-to-charity-shop">owned-given-to-charity-shop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1581504214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4101004840226350766">I was given this book by a friend so didn't choose it as such. The image on the cover and title do not seem to fit with the material covered in the book. It followed 2 characters, Sandra, a 30ish year old woman. who's pregnant but no longer with the baby's father and Julian, an 80ish year old man. who's come over from Argentina to Spain to following up some information about Nazis that his friend Salva has written to him about. Salva and Julia were in Mauthausen concentration camp during WWII an</span>
  <span id="freeText4101004840226350766" style="display:none">I was given this book by a friend so didn't choose it as such. The image on the cover and title do not seem to fit with the material covered in the book. It followed 2 characters, Sandra, a 30ish year old woman. who's pregnant but no longer with the baby's father and Julian, an 80ish year old man. who's come over from Argentina to Spain to following up some information about Nazis that his friend Salva has written to him about. Salva and Julia were in Mauthausen concentration camp during WWII and held captive and tortured by the Nazis that Salva has discovered. Salva and Julian have been part of a group intent on bringing Nazis to trial since the end of WWII. They are both retired from official roles doing that but can never quite stop the search - hence Julian's trip.<br /><br />I was disturbed on a few occasions during the book by the all too vivid descriptions of the torture that occurred in the WWII camp. I really should have stopped reading at that point but did get myself invested in the characters of Sandra and Julian so ploughed on hoping for a satisfactory conclusion. There was none.<br /><br />In fact much of what happened was so far fetched and disjointed that it was hard to get immersed in the story other than wishing for a good conclusion. At one point Julian was attacked by a young 'minder' thug who was part of the Nazi 'Brotherhood' and warned that if he carried on seeing Sandra he would be killed. Julian carried on seeing Sandra in the same way as before with no great attempt at doing so more carefully. And yet there was no more violence against him which made no sense. Julian entered various properties and took things and yet the owners of these properties didn't see fit to increase security, lock doors, set traps or keep a closer eye on things. These and many other points within the story were just so unbelievable. <br /><br />I don't think the translation helped a great deal as one got the impression it was done by Google Translate with figures of speech apparently being translated literally which made little sense in English.<br /><br />A disappointing read with no real conclusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4101004840226350766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_406557201" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406557201" />
    <a title="Joanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4979664-joanne"><img alt="Joanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305281450p2/4979664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406557201?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanne" href="/user/show/4979664-joanne">Joanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846881855" href="/book/show/13512198-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406557201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8870993609656686588">With its romantic sounding title and beautiful cover, you could be forgiven for thinking that this is a gentle romantic novel about a young woman trying to figure out her life. It isn't, it is a dark, intriguing and thought-provoking thriller that draws you in and keeps you in suspense. <br/><br/>Sandra is a young, frivolous woman, who is pregnant, has left her job and partner, and is living in her sister's villa on the Costa Brava, while working out her next move. While on the beach one day, feeling ill,</span>
  <span id="freeText8870993609656686588" style="display:none">With its romantic sounding title and beautiful cover, you could be forgiven for thinking that this is a gentle romantic novel about a young woman trying to figure out her life. It isn't, it is a dark, intriguing and thought-provoking thriller that draws you in and keeps you in suspense. <br /><br />Sandra is a young, frivolous woman, who is pregnant, has left her job and partner, and is living in her sister's villa on the Costa Brava, while working out her next move. While on the beach one day, feeling ill, she is comforted by an elderly Norwegian couple who live nearby, and they become friends. Enter Julian, an elderly survivor of the Mauthausen Nazi concentration camp, who has been drawn back to Spain from his home in Argentina, by his friend Salva. Together they have been tracing Nazi war criminals and Salva has discovered a couple living nearby, but when Julian arrives in Spain, Salva has already died. <br /><br />The book is told in the first person, alternating between Julian and Sandra, as this unlikely couple become friends and together seek to confirm the identity of the Nazis living in this beautiful part of Spain. It's a fairly slow read, and the suspense builds as both put themselves in danger to achieve their aims and seek justice and retribution. <br /><br />The book is beautifully written and very well translated. The stunning setting of the novel is somewhat at odds with the atrocities committed by those who live there, and indeed one of the main themes is whether they should be able to live out their lives in such peace and beauty after the crimes they committed. <br /><br />I have to admit that I didn't expect the ending, and was perhaps initially disappointed as the suspense was building so dramatically, but the more I think about it, the more the ending does seem right. And the most important thing is that this book does keep you thinking long after you've finished it. I'd probably rate it 3.5 overall, but it deserves to be rounded up for preciously that reason.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8870993609656686588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14080590174851418593">I really enjoyed this book.   <span id="freeText14080590174851418593" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. The fact that it is narrated in first person,divided in Chapters and that in each one, the two main characters, Juliàn and Sandra, have a part where they speak it's really interesting, you can read about two points of view of the same events.<br /><p>I think this novel is a fashinating example of when the present and the past collide.</p><br /><p>Juliàn is an elderly survivor of the Mauthausen Nazi concentration camp, who suffers from hear disease but goes all the way from Argentina to Spain because his friend Salva passed away and left him a letter, with his last, important, discover. They dedicated all their life tracing Nazi war criminals and Salva has discovered a couple of Nazis of their age living the last years of their life surrounded by richness and lux. When Juliàn gets the letter, it is already too late. His friend has already died but Juliàn wants to continue his search. It's here when Sandra's life collides with Juliàn's. She's a 30 yeard old pregnant woman who doesn't love the father of her son, Santi. She left both Santi and her job and now leaves, all alone, in her sister's villa, on the Costa Brava. One day, while she is at the beach, she starts feeling dizzy and a kind old man and his wife help her not fainting. They are Fredrick and Karin Christensen. But are they as sweet and kind as they want to look like? Sandra is soon going to discover that danger and evil can hide where no one's ever going to expect. Sandra and Juliàn's lives are going to cross, and nothing will ever be the same. </p><br /><p> I didn't expect such a final, I must admit it, but overall I enjoyed it too. I really recommend this book to the lovers of The Book Thief. That book is one of my favourite books of all time, and this is not half as well written and beautiful as the one by Zusak, but they both taught me a lot.</p> <br />Valeria<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_378054711" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/378054711" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3652044-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485866417p2/3652044.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378054711?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/3652044-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846881855" href="/book/show/13512198-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3652044-ian?shelf=a-kindle">a-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3652044-ian?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378054711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11531879811541813419">Julian, an 80 something Spanish Republican concentration camp survivor and sometime Nazi hunter is drawn from Argentina to Spain by a letter from his friend and fellow survivor Salva. Once in Spain he meets Sandra a 30 year old newly pregnant woman who has been befriended by an elderly Norwegian couple who Julian suspects are ex camp guards who tortured, abused and killed lots of people during the Nazi period of terror. Together, this odd couple discover a whole nest of Nazis, both ancient and m</span>
  <span id="freeText11531879811541813419" style="display:none">Julian, an 80 something Spanish Republican concentration camp survivor and sometime Nazi hunter is drawn from Argentina to Spain by a letter from his friend and fellow survivor Salva. Once in Spain he meets Sandra a 30 year old newly pregnant woman who has been befriended by an elderly Norwegian couple who Julian suspects are ex camp guards who tortured, abused and killed lots of people during the Nazi period of terror. Together, this odd couple discover a whole nest of Nazis, both ancient and modern, and the plot centres on this discovery and what to do about it. I found it all a bit of a struggle. It is a Spanish bestseller BUT I supect this English version suffers badly from a rather literal and soulless translation. Having studied Spanish, it was fairly easy to spot many examples of a literal translation that just didn't work in English. Whilst this spoilt the flow of this potentially interesting story, the main flaw for me was that it was just too unbelievable in terms of plot development - at times it resembled a farce as the two main protagonists continually met in public but in secret in the small town where the action takes place without being spotted by the hordes of Nazis and their sympathisers. I also didn't find the character of Sandra particularly credible - a newly pregnant woman continually risking her life (and crucially her unborn baby) for a cause that she seemed to have no firm belief in.....I don't think so. Trying to present her as being at a crossroads in her life and searching for meaning just didn't wash.........maybe it was the translation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11531879811541813419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5138822003068536123" style="display:none">Brilliant book. This was a surprise. When I began reading, I thought it would be just another book about Nazi hunters and justice. <div id="review_402877472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402877472" />
    <a title="Damaskcat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat"><img alt="Damaskcat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395844674p2/6945307.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/402877472?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damaskcat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damaskcat" href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat">Damaskcat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846881855" href="/book/show/13512198-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer402877472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4511656499192440515">Sandra is pregnant and is trying to decide what to do with her life while she stays in her sister’s holiday home on the Spanish coast. When she is feeling ill on the beach one day Fredrik and Karin, a Norwegian couple help her and subsequently befriend her.<br/><br/> She also meets – apparently randomly – an elderly man called Julian and they become friends. But things are not what they seem and Julian has deliberately befriended Sandra. Julian is a former concentration camp inmate and has made it his lif</span>
  <span id="freeText4511656499192440515" style="display:none">Sandra is pregnant and is trying to decide what to do with her life while she stays in her sister’s holiday home on the Spanish coast. When she is feeling ill on the beach one day Fredrik and Karin, a Norwegian couple help her and subsequently befriend her.<br /><br /> She also meets – apparently randomly – an elderly man called Julian and they become friends. But things are not what they seem and Julian has deliberately befriended Sandra. Julian is a former concentration camp inmate and has made it his life’s work to track down former Nazis and bring them to justice and Fredrik and Karin are former concentration camp guards.<br /><br />I found this book compelling reading. It is told by Sandra and Julian in alternate sections and they both have distinctive voices. I liked the way the tensions build up as Sandra starts to think there is something sinister about Fredrick and Karin and their friends and they seem to be taking over her life and manipulating her every thought and action. I enjoyed the way Sandra developed as a character throughout the story. I don’t always like novels in translation but I felt this one was skilfully done.<br /><br />The friendships between Sandra and Julian and between Sandra and the Norwegian couple are well realised and convincing. I felt all the characters – even the minor ones – were well drawn and I thought the ending was perfect and satisfying. I recommend this book to anyone who wants a novel which is a bit different.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4511656499192440515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Laura Macdonald" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4762539-laura-macdonald"><img alt="Laura Macdonald" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515429903p2/4762539.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Macdonald" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Macdonald" href="/user/show/4762539-laura-macdonald">Laura Macdonald</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846882432" href="/book/show/17399338-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer683271600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17586768293120102686">This is a truly awful book. I haven't read a book which was so boring, so repetitive and so badly written since I made the mistake of reading '50 Shades of Grey' just to see what all the fuss was about. I say 'read' but I listened to most of this book as an audible download. The plot had so much promise, but the writing lets it down. I listened to this as I walked my dog, usually through woods or in cliff paths and found myself talking to myself or laughing out loud at the terrible prose, ensuri</span>
  <span id="freeText17586768293120102686" style="display:none">This is a truly awful book. I haven't read a book which was so boring, so repetitive and so badly written since I made the mistake of reading '50 Shades of Grey' just to see what all the fuss was about. I say 'read' but I listened to most of this book as an audible download. The plot had so much promise, but the writing lets it down. I listened to this as I walked my dog, usually through woods or in cliff paths and found myself talking to myself or laughing out loud at the terrible prose, ensuring that anyone who overheard me probably thought I was a fruitcake. The heroine was a selfish, one dimensional, boring, banal creature and I really couldn't care less about her outcome. Julian, the elderly hero, was written with a little but more flair and I was vaguely interested in him. The 'baddies' were just blah, unbelievable and stereotyped. The book could have been condensed into a third of the length and still would probably have contained far too much inane, pointless dialogue and descriptions. I gave up halfway through (life is just too short for crap like this) and skipped to the end which was just as awful. Oh and whoever decided to give the Spanish barman at the hotel a Yorkshire accent and the Spanish hotel detective, a Scouse accent deserves a prize for stupidity. I tried to forgive this book on the basis that it may have been a bad translation, but it really is unforgivable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17586768293120102686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1995368971506886759">I wasn't quite sure what to make of this book initially. I was expecting a book about Nazi-hunting to be gritty, but in fact the writing in this is quirky and amusing at times. It doesn't belittle the horrors that were experienced in concentration camps at all, but it pokes fun at what may have become of some of the perpetrators and raises some important points about our own lifestyles and choices. It takes quite a long time to reach a conclusion, and I did wonder what could possibly happen in t</span>
  <span id="freeText1995368971506886759" style="display:none">I wasn't quite sure what to make of this book initially. I was expecting a book about Nazi-hunting to be gritty, but in fact the writing in this is quirky and amusing at times. It doesn't belittle the horrors that were experienced in concentration camps at all, but it pokes fun at what may have become of some of the perpetrators and raises some important points about our own lifestyles and choices. It takes quite a long time to reach a conclusion, and I did wonder what could possibly happen in the last half of the book as the Nazis were tracked down so quickly, but overall it was quite a refreshing read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1995368971506886759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review704816399">
  <td colspan="2">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynn" href="/user/show/15265939-lynn">Lynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846881855" href="/book/show/13512198-the-scent-of-lemon-leaves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15265939-lynn?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15265939-lynn?shelf=holocaust">holocaust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15265939-lynn?shelf=jewish-lit">jewish-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer910834572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3420145435488368549">3.5 stars. So much of the story was so improbable: an elderly Holocaust survivor teams up with a pregnant young woman to expose a cache of ex-Nazis, that at times the story was exasperating. The plot plods along at times and some of the twists are almost silly. And what was with the obscure title? The word "lemon" is never mentioned in the entire book. An interesting twist on Holocaust fiction but I've read better. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9517688566102800075">I really liked this book, it was not at all what I was expecting with the lives of an old man out to seek revenge, crossing the path of a young woman hiding away from her responsibilities.<br/><br/>The woman at times I found hard to get along with almost felt like she was acting childlike but by the end of the story she had matured so much that I feel it was probably the authors intention all along so you could clearly see how she much her character had changed<br/><br/>A book worth checking out.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('990C3Y7imvdMSrAexg0/IhvM1EHmozdblaK3tg+V4hxQPyeD7v4o+qsS0ErxXWhnuMcMYA5FtDDvSEGoX6vWyw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3dhQPNFmIZMUBSy6DForIz8Up5FNU107hvq6pCxZ/VZ6OnVisXqTnvNdTO47CnxmnB9/sKW13lD8EEy6fGfJgQ==')})

Le ore di scuola sono uno strazio, i professori “una specie protetta che speri si estingua definitivamente”. \nCosì, quando arriva un nuovo supplente di storia e filosofia, lui si prepara ad accoglierlo con cinismo e palline inzuppate di saliva. Ma questo giovane insegnante è diverso: una luce gli brilla negli occhi quando sprona gli studenti a cercare il proprio sogno. Leo ha un nemico che lo atterrisce: il bianco. \nIl bianco è l’assenza, tutto ciò che ha a che fare con la privazione e la perdita è bianco. \nIl rosso invece è il colore dell’amore, della passione, del sangue; rosso è il colore dei capelli di Beatrice. Perché un sogno Leo ce l’ha e si chiama Beatrice, anche se lei ancora non lo sa. Leo ha anche una realtà, Silvia, una presenza affidabile e serena. \nQuando scopre che Beatrice è ammalata e che la malattia ha qualcosa a che fare con quel bianco che tanto lo spaventa, Leo dovrà scavare a fondo dentro di sé, sanguinare e rinascere, per capire che i sogni non possono morire e trovare il coraggio di credere in qualcosa di più grande.<\/span>\n  <a Fai be<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3814072486652617973\" style=\"display:none\">Fai bei sogni è la storia di un segreto celato in una busta per quarant\'anni. La storia di un bambino, e poi di un adulto, che imparerà ad affrontare il dolore più grande, la perdita della mamma, e il mostro più insidioso: il timore di vivere. Fai bei sogni è dedicato a quelli che nella vita hanno perso qualcosa. Un amore, un lavoro, un tesoro. E rifiutandosi di accettare la realtà, finiscono per smarrire se stessi. Come il protagonista di questo romanzo. Uno che cammina sulle punte dei piedi e a testa bassa perché il cielo lo spaventa, e anche la terra. Fai bei sogni è soprattutto un libro sulla verità e sulla paura di conoscerla. Immergendosi nella sofferenza e superandola, ci ricorda come sia sempre possibile buttarsi alle spalle la sfiducia per andare al di là dei nostri limiti. Massimo Gramellini ha raccolto gli slanci e le ferite di una vita priva del suo appiglio più solido. Una lotta incessante contro la solitudine, l\'inadeguatezza e il senso di abbandono, raccontata con passione e delicata ironia. Il sofferto traguardo sarà la conquista dell\'amore e di un\'esistenza piena e autentica, che consentirà finalmente al protagonista di tenere i piedi per terra senza smettere di alzare gli occhi al Chiusa nella sua stanza, con il tepore del sole estivo ancora sulla pelle, Margherita si sente come ogni adolescente: un\'equilibrista su un filo sospeso nel vuoto. Solo l\'amore dei genitori, della straordinaria nonna Teresa, del fratellino le consentono di lanciarsi, di camminare su quel filo, di mostrarsi al mondo e provare a diventare grande con le sue forze. Ma un giorno Margherita ascolta un messaggio in segreteria telefonica. È suo padre: annuncia che non tornerà più a casa. Per Margherita si spalanca il vuoto sotto i piedi. Ancora non sa che sarà proprio attraversando questo doloroso smarrimento che a poco a poco si trasformerà in una donna, proprio come una splendida perla fiorisce nell\'ostrica in seguito all\'attacco di un predatore marino. Perché questo è il segreto del dolore: sa dove si nasconde la vita e se ne nutre per farle crescere le ali. Sia Mai che la madre si riferiscono a lei come la &quot;Strega dell\'Ovest&quot;, ma nel momento in cui la nonna le rivela di possedere realmente dei poteri magici, Mai rimane incredula e diffidente. Immerse nella natura incontaminata del Giappone più remoto, nonna e nipote passano insieme settimane meravigliose in raccoglimento, lontane dalla frenesia della vita di città, a lavorare nell\'orto, raccogliere erbe selvatiche e cucinare, oltre a dedicarsi, naturalmente, a quelli che sono, secondo la nonna, i rudimenti di base per una giovane strega. A questa storia catartica e rivelatrice, negli anni, l\'autrice ha voluto aggiungere tre brevi racconti che ne riprendono i personaggi e l\'ambientazione e che proponiamo fedelmente nella presente Paolo shrewdly fights his way out of an earthquake-striken Bagnara to start anew in Sicily. Ignazio II rejects his one true love to fulfill his destiny as the head of a trading empire. Not to be outdone by the men, the Florio women unapologetically demand their place outside the restraints of caring mothers, alluring mistresses, or wounded wives. Giula, though only a mistress, is fiercely intelligent and wins over politicians and businessmen alike. Angelina, born a bastard, charts her own future against the wishes of her father.\n\nIn this epic yet intimate tale of power, passion, and revenge, the rise and fall of a family taps into the universal desire to become more than who we are born as. <\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2008863315118279757\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n Ad attenderla all\'aeroporto, Gojko, poeta bosniaco, amico fratello, amore mancato, che ai tempi festosi delle Olimpiadi invernali del 1984 traghettò Gemma verso l\'amore della sua vita, Diego, il fotografo di pozzanghere.\nIl romanzo racconta la storia di questo amore, una storia di ragazzi farneticanti che si rincontrano oggi, giovani sprovveduti, invecchiati in un dopoguerra recente. Una storia d\'amore appassionata, imperfetta come gli amori veri.\nMa anche la storia di una maternità cercata, negata, risarcita. Il cammino misterioso di una nascita che fa piazza pulita della scienza, della biologia, e si addentra nella placenta preistorica di una Guerra che mentre uccide procrea.\nIn questo grande affresco di tenebra e luce, in questo romanzo intimo e sociale, le voci di quei ragazzi si accordano e si frantumano nel continuo rimando tra il ventre di Gemma e il ventre della città dilaniata. Ma l\'avventura di Gemma e Diego è anche la storia di tutti noi, perché Margaret Mazzantini ha scritto un coraggioso romanzo contemporaneo. Di pace e di guerra.\nLa pace è l\'aridità fumosa di un Occidente flaccido di egoismi, perso nella salamoia del benessere. La guerra è quella di una donna che ingaggia contro la natura una battaglia estrema e oltraggiosa. L\'assedio di Sarajevo diventa l\'assedio di ogni personaggio di questa vicenda di non eroi scaraventati dal calcio della Storia in un destino che sembra in attesa di loro come un tiratore scelto. Il cammino intimo di un uomo e di una donna verso un figlio, il loro viaggio di iniziazione alla paternità e alla maternità diventa un travaglio epico, una favola dura come l\'ingiustizia, luminosa come un miracolo.\nDopo Non ti muovere, con una scrittura che è cifra inconfondibile di identità letteraria, Margaret Mazzantini ci regala un romanzo-mondo, opera trascinante e di forte impegno etico, spiazzante come un thriller, emblematica come una parabola. Una catarsi che dimostra come attraverso tutto il male della Storia possa erompere lo stupore smagato, sereno, di un nuovo principio.\nUna specie di avvento che ha il volto mobile, le membra lunghe e ancora sgraziate, l\'ombrosità e gli slanci di un figlio di oggi chiamato Pietro.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"18051214576343426360\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
